### Question 47: I have 112 credits from Fulbright and 16 credits from EL. Can I graduate?  
### Answer: 

To graduate with an undergraduate degree from Fulbright, a student must earn a minimum of 128 credit hours. You have 112 credits from Fulbright and 16 credits from EL, which totals 128 credits. Therefore, you can graduate. The Experiential Learning Program (ELP) credits count toward your graduation requirement, as stated in the context. The ELP requires all full-time, undergraduate, degree-seeking students to complete at least 04 credits and a maximum of 12 credits as a graduation requirement. Since you have completed the minimum required 16 credits through the ELP, you meet the necessary criteria for graduation. The references provided in the context are relevant to answering this question, as they outline the specific requirements for earning a degree from Fulbright University, including the role of elective and experiential learning credits. The information about the ELP, electives, and the total credit requirement is directly applicable to determining whether you can graduate.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 20]
count toward elective or major requirements (upon advisor approval). Fulbright’s Experiential Learning Program (ELP) exists to create, standardize, and facilitate academic credit-bearing experiential learning experiences. All full-time, undergraduate, degree- seeking students must complete at least 04 credits and a maximum of 12 credits under the ELP as a graduation requirement. Current ELP streams are housed within Academic Affairs (AA), Career Services (CS), and Center for Entrepreneurship and Innovation (CEI), where each team is responsible for administrative and academic duties of their respective stream(s). The ELP operates within Fulbright’s undergraduate program’s standard operating procedures and is developed in consultation with undergraduate program leadership and faculty. For more details, please refer here https://onestop.fulbright.edu.vn/s/article/Experiential-Learning- Program 13.5  Electives To complete the degree, students are free to take elective courses from the Course Catalogue. While the

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 7]
of credit hours a student successfully completes with a grade of D or higher for letter grade options and a Pass for Pass/No Pass options. Attempted credits are the credit hours students enroll in and are recorded in the transcript, regardless of whether they complete the courses or pass them. ### Question 48: I have received an offer to attend an international conference but lack funding. What school funds can I apply for?  
### Answer: 

Fulbright University Vietnam has a student research fund which supports student’s research projects, including capstone projects. Students can apply for funding from this fund to cover the costs associated with attending the international conference. Additionally, students can also explore other funding opportunities available through external organizations, grants, or scholarships that might be relevant to their field of study and the purpose of attending the conference. It is important to prepare a well-structured proposal detailing the conference's relevance to the student's academic and career goals, the expected outcomes, and how the funding will be used efficiently. Before applying for any funding, students should also consult with their academic advisors to ensure that the conference aligns with their academic plan and to get advice on the application process.

### Question 49: What is the maximum number of credits I can transfer from another university after officially enrolling at Fulbright?  
### Answer: 

The maximum number of credits that can be transferred and credited to a Fulbright undergraduate degree is 64 credit hours.

### Question 50: In a regular semester, can I take only 2 courses? If so, how will my tuition fees be affected?  
### Answer: 

In a regular semester, you can take fewer than 12 credits, but you need to submit a Petition for Alternative Course Load form to the Registrar's Office. This form must be approved and signed by your Academic/Major Advisor before submission. The request form is necessary because the typical full-time course load is 16 credit hours per term, and students are required to register for no fewer than 12 credit hours and no more than 20 credit hours per term. Taking fewer than 12 credits may affect your financial aid eligibility and no reduction in tuition is granted to students whose course withdrawal results in fewer than 12 academic credits. Therefore, while you can take only 2 courses (8 credit hours), your tuition fees will not be reduced, and you should be aware that this may impact your financial aid eligibility.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 7]
circumstances (see Section 12), and it requires supporting documentation as well as the authorization of course instructor(s), the student’s academic/major advisor, and the Registrar’s Office. In the case of approved exceptional circumstances, tuition credit will be considered and follow the “Fees & Charges Guide” for undergraduate students. No reduction in tuition is granted to students whose course withdrawal results in fewer than 12 academic credits.  Students should be aware that course withdrawals may affect their financial aid eligibility if resulting in fewer than the minimum credits for full-time enrollment. • Waitlist: Each course at Fulbright has a maximum capacity. The registration system on the Fulbright One Stop portal allows students to join a waitlist for courses that are full. Should space become available, students will be enrolled in the course in order of their appearance on the waitlist during the registration or Add/Drop time. When a waitlisted student is added to a course, it is the

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 7]
maintaining the full-time enrollment status of registering for a minimum of 12 credits per term. • Course Withdrawal: There are two Withdrawal periods per term. The first period starts after 4:00 PM Friday, Week 2 to 4:00 PM Friday, Week 4. During this time, students can request to withdraw from the course without any consequence. The second period starts after 4:00 PM Friday, Week 4 to 4:00 PM Friday, Week 8. Attempted credits and a “W” grade will be recorded on the transcript for the course(s) from which students withdraw in this period. This grade does not affect a student’s GPA. In order to withdraw from a course, students need to submit the Course Withdrawal form to the Registrar’s Office, following the above timeline. A student who withdraws from a course beyond the halfway point of that course (end of week 4 for an 8-week course or end of week 8 for a full-term course) automatically receives a grade of ‘F’, which will affect the student’s GPA. ### Question 51: Can I pursue 3 majors?  
### Answer: 

No, the policy explicitly states that students must complete all requirements for each major when pursuing a double major. The text does not provide information on pursuing three majors simultaneously. The policy mentions that students pursuing a double major must complete all requirements for each major, and it also explains the rules for double-counting courses between two majors or a major and a minor. However, it does not extend this information to triple majors. Therefore, based on the provided information, it is not possible to pursue three majors simultaneously under the described policy. The maximum number of majors a student can pursue, according to the given context, is two.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 20]
major or minor requirements must be taken for a letter grade. Students can claim a maximum of 8 credits (2 courses) toward both their Exploratory and major requirements. During their final year of study, students have the option to either complete a capstone project, which will count for 8 credits in their major area of study, or fulfill those credits with additional advanced coursework. Students pursuing a double major must complete all requirements for each major. If two majors (or two minors, or a major and a minor) share cross- listed or tagged1 courses, up to 8 credits (two courses) can be used to satisfy both sets of requirements. This limit is per each pair of majors (or major and minor) and does not restrict the total number of double-counted credits or courses a student can claim. For example, a student can major in both A and B and minor in C with a total of 6 double-counted courses: two in A and B, two in B and C, and two in A and C. This rule does not apply to courses that are not cross-listed or

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 20]
13.2 and 13.3). Additionally, any particular course can only be used to satisfy at most two requirements. For instance, if course X is cross-listed between major A and major B and tagged by minor C, then X can be used to fulfill the requirements of major A and major B, or major A and minor C, or major B and minor C. Triple counting is not allowed. 13.9  Maximal Length of Study Fulbright follows MOET regulations, which state that the maximum time to complete the program cannot exceed double the standard duration. In other words, students have a maximum of 8 years to complete their studies.

### Question 52: How can I change my major declaration?  
### Answer: 

To change your major declaration, you should follow the specific procedures outlined by the university. Typically, this involves meeting with the major coordinator and the Dean's Office to discuss your interest in changing majors and to ensure that you meet the prerequisites and requirements for the new major. Here are the general steps you should take:

1. **Research the New Major**: Make sure you understand the requirements for the new major, including any additional courses you need to take, prerequisites, and any specific policies or requirements unique to that major.

2. **Meet with the Major Coordinator**: Contact the coordinator for the major you are interested in and schedule an appointment to discuss your interest in changing majors. The coordinator can provide you with detailed information about the major, including any additional courses or policies you need to be aware of.

3. **Petition Process (if necessary)**: Some universities may require you to submit a petition to change your major. This petition should outline your academic background, your reasons for wanting to change majors, and how you plan to meet the requirements of the new major.

4. **Academic Advisor Consultation**: Your current academic advisor can also provide guidance and support throughout the process. They can help you understand the implications of changing majors on your academic plan and ensure that you are meeting all university requirements.

5. **Dean's Office Approval**: In some cases, approval from the Dean's Office may be required to officially change your major. This step ensures that you are following the correct procedures and meeting all necessary requirements.

6. **Update Your Academic Record**: Once your change of major is approved, make sure to update your academic record with the registrar's office to reflect your new major status.

Remember, changing majors is a significant decision and should be approached thoughtfully. Consider factors such as your career goals, academic interests, and the time and effort required to complete the new major's requirements. It's also a good idea to discuss your decision with trusted mentors, such as academic advisors or faculty members, who can provide valuable insights and support.

The specific procedures and requirements for changing your major can vary by institution, so it's important to consult the relevant academic policies and guidelines provided by your university.

### Question 53: What is the process of delaying my payment?  
### Answer: 

To delay payment, a student must contact Student Financial Services. They will attempt to determine the circumstances and request a timely response from the student. If the student anticipates being unable to clear the account on time, they should meet with the Student Financial Services team as soon as possible to request assistance and alternative solutions. The student should understand that being placed on a payment plan or receiving financial aid does not automatically delay payment; they must discuss their situation with Student Financial Services to explore options. Additionally, students should be aware that delaying payment can lead to being placed on a Leave of Absence status, which prevents them from registering for new courses, participating in classes, or working in a Work-Study Program during the current term. If a student is granted a Leave of Absence, they must return and register for classes using the One-Stop platform within fourteen (14) working days of their return, or they may face further administrative actions.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 15]
Student Financial Services to request a late and/or an extension of tuition fee payment. Before placing a student in this type of absence, the Student Financial Services team will attempt to determine the circumstances and request a timely response from the student. With this absence status, students are unable to register for new course(s) during the registration period, participate in classes or a Work-Study Program in the current term. A student will only be reinstated as “Active” status if the outstanding balance is clear. If the student anticipates being unable to clear the account on time, the student should meet with the Student Financial Services team as soon as possible to request assistance and alternative solutions. After the approved period of absence, a student is put on Administrative Leave of Absence (Admin LOA) for a maximum of one term if the Registrar’s Office receives no response of return confirmation or no registration in the returning term. ### Question 55: How many courses can I take in total?  
### Answer: 

The total number of courses a student can take is not explicitly stated in the given contexts. However, the contexts do provide some relevant information:

- Students must take major or minor requirements for a letter grade.
- Students can claim a maximum of 8 credits (2 courses) toward both their Exploratory and major requirements.
- Students pursuing a double major must complete all requirements for each major.
- Up to 8 credits (two courses) can be double-counted between two majors or a major and a minor.
- Double-counting rules allow for a total of 6 double-counted courses across multiple majors and minors, as illustrated in the example.

Given these points, the total number of courses a student can take is not directly specified. The maximum number of courses that can be double-counted is 6, but this does not equate to the total number of courses a student can take. The total number of courses a student can take depends on the overall credit requirements for the degree (128 credits in this case) and the distribution of those credits across various requirements (Exploratory, major, minor, etc.).

Therefore, the total number of courses a student can take is determined by dividing the total credit requirement (128 credits) by the average number of credits per course (typically 4 credits per course). This gives:

128 credits / 4 credits per course = 32 courses.

So, the student can take a total of 32 courses to meet the 128-credit requirement, considering the possibility of double-counting up to 6 courses.

The references provided do not directly answer the question of the total number of courses a student can take, but the calculation based on the standard credit per course provides a reasonable estimate. The contexts do not specify any additional restrictions or allowances that would alter this basic calculation.

In summary, a student can take a total of 32 courses to meet the 128-credit requirement, with the possibility of double-counting up to 6 courses. The references provided do not offer additional information to adjust this calculation.

### Question 58: How can I audit a course?  
### Answer: 

To audit a course, you must obtain permission from the instructor. You must also meet the prerequisites for the course. Audited courses do not count towards your degree requirements and you will not receive a grade. Audited courses are usually noted as "AU" on your transcript.

### Question 59: If I'm going for a double major then how many courses can be double count maximum?  
### Answer: 

In the context provided, students pursuing a double major can have up to 8 credits (which equates to two courses) double-counted toward both their majors. This rule applies to cross-listed or tagged courses between the two majors. However, this 8-credit limit is per each pair of majors, meaning it does not restrict the total number of double-counted credits or courses a student can claim across all pairs of majors they are pursuing. For example, if a student is majoring in both A and B and has a minor in C, they can double-count up to 8 credits between A and B, another 8 credits between B and C, and another 8 credits between A and C, resulting in a total of 24 double-counted credits (or 6 double-counted courses) across all pairs. It's important to note that this rule does not apply to courses that are not cross-listed or tagged, and courses cannot be triple-counted.

### Question 62: Why and how am I getting academic suspension?  
### Answer: 

You are getting academic suspension because you have failed to fulfill all the requirements of your Learning Contract while on Academic Probation. The process involves receiving an Academic Warning, which is the first level of intervention for students not making satisfactory progress. If you receive three official warnings, you may be placed on Academic Probation, which is the second level of intervention. If you fail to meet the requirements of your updated Learning Contract while on Academic Probation, you may be placed on Academic Suspension. The Registrar's Office informs you and schedules an Academic Progress Meeting where a Learning Contract is updated with specific conditions. If you fail to meet these conditions, the Dean's Office will establish conditions for your return to Fulbright. You may not visit the campus without permission during the suspension period, which typically lasts for one term or one academic year. You may be suspended a maximum of two times. A third suspension will result in the cancellation of your enrolment in the program, and you must apply for re-admission, providing a letter explaining the reasons for your suspensions and the measures you have taken to address them. The re-admission decision is made by the Dean's Office in consultation with faculty and staff, and students who are re-admitted must also re-apply for financial aid.

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 2]

### Question 63: How does the P/NP grade work?  
### Answer: 

The P/NP grade system allows students to take up to 8 credits per academic year on a Pass/No Pass basis. To do this, students must submit a Petition to Elect Pass/No Pass Grade form to the Registrar’s Office before a specific deadline (typically Friday of Week 4 in a 16-week term). Once a student elects the P/NP grade option for a course, it cannot be changed back to a letter grade. 

Here are the key points about how the P/NP grade works:

1. **Limitation**: Students can take a maximum of 8 credits (typically 2 courses, 4 credits each) on a P/NP basis per academic year.

2. **Deadline**: The petition must be submitted to the Registrar’s Office before a specific deadline (Friday of Week 4 in a 16-week term).

3. **Irreversible Decision**: Once a student chooses P/NP for a course, they cannot switch back to a letter grade.

4. **Applicability**: P/NP grades do not apply to core courses and cannot be used to count toward major/minor requirements.

5. **Grade Conversion**: The Registrar’s Office converts the final letter grade submitted by the instructor to a P/NP grade at the end of the term. 
   - A grade of 'C-' or higher is counted as a Pass (P).
   - Any grade below a 'C-' is counted as a No Pass (NP).

6. **Transcript Impact**: The NP grade will be shown on the Official Transcript and cannot be used to meet prerequisite requirements for next-level courses.

7. **Prerequisite Use**: Courses graded with a Pass (P) can be used to meet prerequisite requirements for next-level courses.

In summary, the P/NP grade system is a flexible option for students to take certain courses without the pressure of achieving a specific letter grade, while still allowing them to potentially earn credit if they achieve a 'C-' or higher. However, it comes with limitations regarding the number of credits that can be taken this way, the irreversibility of the choice, and restrictions on how these grades can be applied toward degree requirements.

### Question 64: How many courses can I take as P/NP at maximum and how will it contribute to the official transcript GPA?  
### Answer: 

You can take a total of 8 credits (typically 2 courses, 4 credits each) on a Pass/No Pass basis. Pass/No Pass grades do not apply to core courses and cannot be used to count toward major/minor requirements. A grade of 'C-' or higher will be counted as a Pass, and courses graded with a Pass grade can be used to meet prerequisite requirements for next-level courses. Any grade below a 'C-' will be counted as a No Pass, and no credit is granted for this result. The NP grade will be shown on the Official Transcript, but courses with a NP grade cannot be used to meet prerequisite requirements for next-level courses. Pass/No Pass grades are excluded from the GPA calculation.

### Question 65: I've failed the GWP due to personal reasons so will it count toward the 144 maximum credits I can have?  
### Answer: 

The policy on repeating courses states that students are required to repeat core courses if they receive an F grade, and they may repeat any course if they received a grade of 'D+', 'D', 'F', or 'NP'. In your case, since you've failed the GWP (which likely means you received an F grade), you are required to repeat the course. The repeated course will count toward the total attempted credits, which includes all courses regardless of the grade received. Therefore, the credits from the repeated GWP course will count toward the 144 maximum credits you can have. However, it's important to note that the grade point average (GPA) calculation excludes courses with grades of P/NP, I, W, or RP. If you repeat the course and earn a higher grade, only the higher grade will be used in the GPA calculation, while the lower grade will be replaced with an "RP" notation on your transcript. This means that while the course will count toward your total attempted credits, it will not negatively impact your GPA as much as it would have if you hadn't repeated it. Always consult with the Registrar's Office or your academic advisor for the most accurate and personalized advice regarding your academic standing and credit limits.

### Question 66: What and how do I get an Academic Warning?  
### Answer: 

An Academic Warning is usually the first level of intervention for students who are not making satisfactory progress toward their degree and/or who fall below a 2.0 GPA, or for other reasons such as failure of attendance, participation, citizenship, or academic integrity. An Academic Warning is sent out by the Registrar’s Office. The student is required to attend an Academic Progress Meeting during which a Learning Contract will be created with specific conditions tailored to the individual situation. The Registrar's Office will be informed as a matter of record and follow-up. Three official warnings shall result in Disciplinary Action, constituting Academic Probation or Academic Suspension.

### Question 67: How can I make reservations of rooms for personal usage?  
### Answer: 

To make reservations for rooms for personal usage at Fulbright, you would typically follow these steps:

1. Contact the Residential Life Office: Reach out to the Residential Life Office at Fulbright to inquire about the availability of rooms for personal usage during your leave. You can do this by phone, email, or in person.

2. Review Policies: Familiarize yourself with the policies regarding room reservations for personal use during a leave of absence. This may include information on the duration of stay, any fees involved, and any conditions attached to the reservation.

3. Submit a Request: Complete and submit a room reservation request form provided by the Residential Life Office. This form will likely require details such as your name, the dates of your stay, and any special requirements you might have.

4. Provide Proof of Leave: As part of the reservation process, you may be required to provide proof of your leave, such as a letter from the Office of the Registrar or Academic Affairs confirming your leave of absence.

5. Pay Any Fees: If there are fees associated with reserving a room for personal use, make sure to pay them according to the payment schedule provided by the Residential Life Office.

6. Confirm Reservation: Once your request is approved, you will receive a confirmation of your reservation. Make sure to review the confirmation details and understand your obligations during your stay.

7. Check-In: Upon arrival, check in at the Residential Life Office to receive your key and any other necessary information about your stay.

8. Follow Rules and Regulations: Ensure you are aware of and adhere to all rules and regulations of the residence halls, including check-in and check-out times, quiet hours, and any other policies that may apply.

Remember that the specific process may vary depending on the institution's policies and procedures, so it's important to communicate directly with the Residential Life Office at Fulbright for the most accurate and up-to-date information.

### Question 68: Can you provide me with some courses suggestion to take to major in Math?  
### Answer: 

To major in Applied Mathematics, you should start with the foundation courses, which include Linear Algebra, Single Variable Calculus, Introduction to Statistics, and Multivariable Calculus. After completing these foundation courses, you should move on to intermediate courses such as Probability, Differential Equations, Discrete Mathematics, and Numerical Analysis. For advanced study, choose from courses like Advanced Statistics, Statistical Learning, Stochastic Calculus, Numerical Analysis, Optimization, and Partial Differential Equations. Additionally, you should take at least two applied courses from other majors, such as Game Theory from Economics, Signal, Systems, and Control from Engineering, or Introduction to Machine Learning from Computer Science. These applied courses will help you see the practical applications of mathematics in various fields.

It's also important to note that if you're considering graduate school in Economics or Finance, you should ensure a strong mathematical foundation by taking additional courses in calculus, linear algebra, differential equations, and real analysis. Consulting with an academic advisor is crucial to tailor your course selection to your specific interests and career goals within Applied Mathematics.

Regarding the note for students considering graduate school in Economics or Finance, while the Applied Mathematics major provides a solid mathematical foundation, it's essential to also engage with Economics-specific courses like Money and Banking, Economics of Inequality, and Market Design. These courses will complement your mathematical skills with economic theory and analysis, which are crucial for success in Economics or Finance graduate programs.

Lastly, remember that you cannot double count a course for two different requirements. For example, Operations Research can only count for either an advanced or an applied course, not both. Always check with your academic advisor to ensure your course selection meets all major requirements and aligns with your future academic and career plans.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Major Descriptions and Flowcharts_OfficialVersion.pdf, Page: 17]
of areas with applications in Mathematics: • Applied Statistics (Economics, Social Sciences, Mathematical Finance, Bioinformatics…) • Engineering Mathematics (Signal processing, Numerical simulation, Inverse problems…) • Data Science (Machine learning, Artificial intelligence …) Students will take at least 2 advanced courses. Consultation with an academic advisor is required for course selection. ### Question 69: How to declare a major in Computer Science?  
### Answer: 

To formally declare Computer Science as their major, the student must complete at least two Computer Science courses (MATH 202 - Discrete Math is also counted). The specific requirements include completing CS 101: Introduction to Programming, CS 201: Data Structures & Algorithms, MATH 202: Discrete Math, three intermediate courses, CS 302: Algorithms & Theory of Computing, four advanced courses, and two capstone courses (Capstone I and Capstone II) or additional intermediate or advanced courses. These requirements ensure that students gain a strong foundation in computer science, including theoretical knowledge, proficiency in designing systems and applications, and experience in data analysis using modern technologies.

### Question 70: I'm currently under a General Work Program for Experiential Learning but the company do not pay me in any form. How can I get the subsidy from Fulbright University?  
### Answer: 

Fulbright University Vietnam's Experiential Learning Program (ELP) offers students the opportunity to gain academic credit for their experiential learning experiences. However, the ELP does not provide a subsidy for students' compensation while they are working under the General Work Program. The ELP is designed to facilitate academic credit-bearing experiences, not to provide financial support for the work performed.

The ELP requires students to complete a minimum of 4 credits and a maximum of 12 credits, which can count toward elective or major requirements with advisor approval. The program is administered by Academic Affairs (AA), Career Services (CS), and the Center for Entrepreneurship and Innovation (CEI), each responsible for their respective streams.

To participate in the ELP, students must:

1. Identify an appropriate experiential learning opportunity.
2. Work with their academic advisor to ensure the experience aligns with their academic goals and can be approved for credit.
3. Complete the necessary paperwork and documentation to enroll in the ELP course associated with their experience.

Regarding financial compensation, students are responsible for negotiating their own terms with the host organization. Fulbright University Vietnam does not provide a subsidy for students' wages or compensation during their experiential learning placements.

If you are not being paid for your work, you may want to discuss this with the company you are working with to see if there is a possibility of receiving compensation or if there are other forms of support they can provide. Additionally, you may want to speak with Career Services at Fulbright University Vietnam to explore other potential funding sources or to discuss alternative arrangements that could still allow you to earn academic credit through the ELP.

Remember to regularly check the official Fulbright University Vietnam website and resources for any updates or additional information regarding financial support or policies related to the ELP, as these may change over time.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 20]
count toward elective or major requirements (upon advisor approval). All full-time, undergraduate, degree- seeking students must complete at least 04 credits and a maximum of 12 credits under the ELP as a graduation requirement. Current ELP streams are housed within Academic Affairs (AA), Career Services (CS), and Center for Entrepreneurship and Innovation (CEI), where each team is responsible for administrative and academic duties of their respective stream(s). The ELP operates within Fulbright’s undergraduate program’s standard operating procedures and is developed in consultation with undergraduate program leadership and faculty. ### Question 71: Can you give me the process of making a Capstone for graduation?  
### Answer: 

A capstone for graduation, particularly in the context provided, involves a multi-step process that culminates in a significant project demonstrating the student's learning and competency in their field of study. Here's a breakdown of the process:

**1. Planning and Selection:**
   - **Early Consultation:** Students should consult with prospective advisors early in their junior year to discuss and plan their capstone project. This includes selecting a topic that aligns with their interests and the curriculum's learning outcomes.
   - **Project Definition:** Decide on the form of the capstone project (e.g., thesis, artwork, film) based on the major and personal interests. For instance, in Art & Media Studies, it could be a thesis, an art piece, or a film.

**2. Research and Development:**
   - **Literature Review:** Conduct a comprehensive literature review or annotated bibliography of at least five pages (2,000 words) to establish the theoretical and practical foundation of the project.
   - **Initial Planning:** Develop an introduction and outline the project's scope, objectives, and methodology. This step is crucial for guiding the research and production phases.
   - **Advising Meetings:** Regular meetings with advisors to discuss progress, receive feedback, and adjust the project plan as necessary.

**3. Production:**
   - **Capstone II:** This phase focuses on the actual production of the capstone project. This could involve writing the thesis, creating the artwork, or producing the film.
   - **Primary Research:** Encouraged but not extensive fieldwork is advised. The project should demonstrate original critical and creative thinking.

**4. Submission and Evaluation:**
   - **End-of-Term Submission:** Submit a progress report or a combination of materials (e.g., literature review, introduction, questionnaires) that demonstrate successful progress towards the final capstone submission.
   - **Capstone II Completion:** Complete the production of the capstone project, which should be coherent, meaningful, and demonstrate the student's competency in their field.
   - **Evaluation:** The capstone project is evaluated based on criteria such as originality, critical and creative thinking, coherence, and adherence to the project plan.

**5. Reflection and Feedback:**
   - **Reflection:** Students are often required to reflect on their learning process, the challenges faced, and how they overcame them.
   - **Feedback:** Receive feedback from advisors and possibly a committee or external reviewers to refine and finalize the capstone project.

**6. Final Submission:**
   - **Completion:** Ensure all aspects of the capstone project are completed to the satisfaction of the advisors and any relevant committees.
   - **Submission:** Submit the final capstone project, which may include the thesis, artwork, film, or other creative work, along with any required documentation.

**Note:** The specifics of the capstone process can vary by institution and program, so it's important to consult with your academic advisor for detailed guidance tailored to your particular situation.

The provided context outlines the process for a capstone in a broad sense, applicable across various disciplines, with a focus on the steps involved in planning, researching, producing, and submitting a capstone project for graduation. It's a comprehensive process designed to showcase a student's academic and creative achievements over their undergraduate career.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Art & Media Studies Capstone Handbook _v3_210125.pdf, Page: 6]

General Information: A culmination to the student’s curriculum, the capstone is an individual project that demonstrates the principal learning outcomes and competencies of that curriculum in a meaningful and coherent way. The capstone may also draw from relevant extra-curricular activities and practical experience to support the research and realization of the project. The capstone should evidence competency in a primary disciplinary specialization (optionally supported by secondary and tertiary disciplinary areas). In the Art & Media Studies major, the capstone could take the form of a thesis, an art work, or a film. For other kinds of projects, please consult with your prospective advisor(s) early in your junior year to determine the suitability and feasibility of your proposed project. ### Question 72: What are the grades required to get a distinctive graduation?  
### Answer: 

To get a distinctive graduation, students must have their capstone projects graded as Honors. The grading scale for the capstone projects is as follows: Pass, Honors, and No Pass. Students whose capstone is graded Honors will be awarded Graduation with Honors.

### Question 73: How can I graduate with Honor or lie within the top GPA?  
### Answer: 

To graduate with Honors or lie within the top GPA, you must maintain a 3.5 GPA throughout your senior year. This is a requirement for earning Honors for the capstone project. If you fail to maintain this required GPA, your capstone project will be capped at a Pass grade, which means you will not graduate with Honors. It's important to focus on your academic performance during your senior year to meet this criterion. Additionally, you must also meet the eligibility criteria for applying to the capstone in Computer Science, which includes having a Major GPA of 3.5 with no exceptions. Regularly check your GPA and stay in close communication with your academic advisor to ensure you are on track to meet these requirements.

### Question 74: How many courses can I take with P/NP grade in total?  
### Answer: 

A student can take a total of 8 credits (typically 2 courses, 4 credits each) on a Pass/No Pass basis in one academic year.

### Question 75: How many types of absences are there?  
### Answer: 

There are four types of absences: General absences, Military leave, Excused absence due to university-sponsored events/activities, and Emergency.

ATTENDANCE: Fulbright students are expected to fully engage with the courses in which they are enrolled at Fulbright, including classes, seminars, talks, and other keystone events. ### Question 76: How many types of leave of absence are there and how can I have one?  
### Answer: 

There are three types of leave of absence: Personal Leave, Medical Leave, and Administrative Leave of Absence. To have one, you must complete and submit the Undergraduate Leave of Absence form, along with supporting documents, before the last day of class. You should also consult with your Academic Advisor to plan for your learning path before submitting the form. Fulbright permits students in Good Academic Standing to apply for a leave of absence for one to two terms. Normally, a student is not permitted to remain on campus during a period of absence from their studies. To return earlier, you must notify the Registrar’s Office at least eight (08) weeks in advance of the returning term.

### Question 77: How can I report violation of Academic environment anonymously?  
### Answer: 

At Fulbright University Vietnam, if you wish to report a violation of academic integrity or any other academic misconduct anonymously, you should follow the procedures outlined in the university's Code of Academic Integrity. Typically, universities have established channels for reporting such incidents, which may include:

1. **Online Reporting System**: Many universities have an online portal or system where individuals can submit reports anonymously. This system is designed to protect the identity of the reporter while ensuring that the incident is investigated thoroughly.

2. **Confidential Hotline**: Some institutions might offer a confidential hotline that allows individuals to report violations anonymously. This hotline is typically staffed by trained personnel who can take the report and initiate the necessary investigation.

3. **Email**: Universities often provide a dedicated email address for reporting academic integrity violations. This email can be used to submit reports anonymously, ensuring that the reporter's identity remains confidential.

4. **In-Person Reporting**: While this might not be anonymous, some individuals may prefer to report violations in person to a designated official, such as the Dean of Students or the Director of Academic Integrity. In such cases, the university might have protocols in place to protect the reporter's identity to the extent possible.

5. **Student Affairs Office**: The Student Affairs Office or similar departments often handle academic integrity issues. They can provide guidance on how to report violations anonymously.

**Important Considerations**:
- **Documentation**: When reporting, it's important to provide as much detail as possible about the incident, including dates, times, locations, and any evidence that supports the claim.
- **Confidentiality**: Universities typically assure confidentiality to the extent possible, but the extent to which anonymity can be maintained may vary depending on the nature and severity of the incident.
- **Follow-Up**: After submitting a report, it's important to follow up with the university to ensure that the report has been received and is being acted upon.

**Relevant to the Context**:
Given the context provided about Fulbright University Vietnam's Code of Academic Integrity and the mention of generative AI, it's clear that the university takes academic integrity very seriously. The procedures for reporting violations should be detailed in the Code of Academic Integrity document, which likely includes instructions on how to report anonymously. 

**Irrelevant References**:
- The mention of a "Non-Academic Advisor" and "Course Information" does not directly relate to the process of reporting academic integrity violations.
- The reference to "ACADEMIC YEAR 20____ - 20____ TERM" is also irrelevant to the question of how to report violations anonymously.

In summary, to report a violation of academic integrity anonymously at Fulbright University Vietnam, you should refer to the university's Code of Academic Integrity for specific instructions on how to submit a report through the appropriate channels, which may include an online reporting system, a confidential hotline, or a dedicated email address. Always ensure to provide as much detail as possible about the incident and follow up to confirm that the report has been received and is being acted upon.

### Question 80: What are the policies regarding retaking exams or improving grades?  
### Answer: 

Students are required to repeat core courses in the case of receiving the grade F and/or courses counted toward major/minor in the case of receiving a grade below ‘C-’. They may repeat a course if they have received a grade of ‘D+’, ‘D’, ‘F’, or NP for the course or have withdrawn and received a grade of ‘W’. In special cases, a student may request to repeat a course after having received a grade higher than a ‘D+’ following consultation with their academic/major advisor, the course instructor, and the Registrar’s Office. Considerations include course availability and capacity in the next academic term or next academic year. A higher grade will be kept and used in the GPA calculation. The lower grade will be overwritten by the notation “RP”, meaning “repeated”, and remain on the transcript. Credits of the repeated course are counted toward the total attempted credits. A student may not retake the same course for the third time unless they failed the second time or if a specific grade is needed to meet the major requirements. Students shall consult with their Academic/Major Advisor about their program plan if they are considering taking the class for a third time.  

<details>

APPEALS: A student who wishes to dispute a final grade in a course should first discuss the matter with the course instructor(s). If the matter remains unresolved and the student believes there has been an error in grading, bias, or failure to follow published grading policies, the student may file an appeal as follows: • Submit the Review of Final Grade Request form to the Registrar's Office within five (05) business days from the date on which the Registrar's Office posts the final grade for the term. • The Registrar's Office informs the Dean’s Office of the case. After investigation, if the Deans can mediate, no further action is required. Otherwise, the Registrar's Office organizes a panel review with the Dean’s Office for an independent evaluation of the grade. The grade determined after this evaluation shall be the final grade. ### Question 81: How does the university accommodate students with chronic illnesses or personal emergencies that affect attendance?  
### Answer: 

The university acknowledges that students may experience exceptional circumstances, such as exceptional medical circumstances (including hospitalization, injury, illness, or mental health crisis), close bereavement, being a victim of a serious crime, disabilities for which reasonable adjustments are not yet in place, and unforeseeable transport difficulties. For these situations, students are responsible for submitting appropriate documentation and contacting their instructors to initiate arrangements to make up any missed work. Instructors are expected to outline attendance expectations at the beginning of the term, communicate consequences of unexcused absences, allow students to make up missed assignments if the absence is reasonable, and inform students if they are in danger of failing the course due to absences.

Instructors are also encouraged to accommodate students with military leave, university-sponsored events, and other approved absences. Students are expected to request permission for absences at least 24 hours in advance, discuss any unplanned absences with their instructors as soon as possible, and make up any missed assignments according to the instructor's instructions.

For chronic illnesses or personal emergencies that regularly affect attendance, students should work closely with their instructors and the university's Office of the Dean and Deans of Students to ensure that reasonable accommodations are made. This may include flexible deadlines, alternative assessment methods, or other adjustments to the academic program. It's important for students to communicate their needs and provide appropriate documentation to support their requests for accommodations.

In summary, the university encourages open communication between students and instructors, and provides a framework for handling absences due to exceptional circumstances. Students with chronic illnesses or personal emergencies should proactively engage with their instructors and relevant university offices to discuss and arrange accommodations that will allow them to continue their studies effectively.

### Question 82: Are students allowed to use AI tools like ChatGPT for assignments? If so, under what conditions?  
### Answer: 

Students at Fulbright University Vietnam are allowed to use generative AI tools like ChatGPT for their assignments, but they must adhere to strict guidelines to ensure academic integrity and ethical use. Here are the conditions under which AI tools can be used:

1. **Comprehensive Documentation**: Any creative project that incorporates generative AI must include comprehensive documentation. This documentation should cover the objective and scope of AI usage, the specific tools and platforms employed, the process and methodology of AI incorporation, and how ethical and copyright issues are addressed.

2. **Academic Integrity**: The use of generative AI must comply with Fulbright University Vietnam’s Code of Academic Integrity. This means that while AI can be used to assist in the creative process, the final product must be the result of the student's own understanding and work. The AI's contribution must be clearly documented.

3. **IRB Approval**: For research projects involving human subjects, students must obtain Institutional Review Board (IRB) approval before using AI tools. This ensures that the data protection and ethical considerations are properly addressed.

4. **Grading Process**: The use of AI tools will be evaluated during the grading process, which involves a double-marking process by the primary and secondary advisors. The AI's role in the project will be considered, but the final assessment will focus on the student's understanding, creativity, and ability to integrate AI effectively.

5. **Group Projects**: For group projects, the use of AI tools may be considered on a case-by-case basis. The advisors will decide on the approval process, ensuring that the use of AI does not compromise the integrity of the group project.

6. **Ethical and Copyright Issues**: Addressing ethical and copyright concerns is crucial. Students must ensure that the AI-generated content does not infringe on any copyrights and that the ethical implications of using AI are carefully considered and managed throughout the project.

In summary, while students are allowed to use AI tools like ChatGPT for their assignments, they must adhere to strict guidelines regarding documentation, academic integrity, IRB approval (for research projects), and ethical considerations. The use of AI tools is subject to review and approval by the advisors and must not compromise the originality and integrity of the student's work.  

<details>

[Source: VIETNAM STUDIES CAPSTONE GUIDELINES.pdf, Page: 6]

### Question 83: Where can I get support for mental health treatment?  
### Answer: 

The Capstone by Applied Project offers several resources and support mechanisms for mental health treatment. Students can access a Mental Health First Aid Training Program, which provides essential skills and knowledge to support individuals experiencing mental health issues. Additionally, a Community Survey on Mental Health Needs can help identify specific areas of concern within the community, allowing for targeted interventions and support services.

A Public Art Project on Mental Health Themes can also serve as a platform to raise awareness and reduce stigma, while a Resource Guide for Local Mental Health Services offers concrete information on where and how to seek help. Therapeutic Gardening or Nature Programs provide an alternative, accessible form of treatment that can complement traditional mental health services.

Each of these projects requires extensive documentation of the process through which they were developed, ensuring transparency and accountability. Furthermore, the final Evaluation Report for the Capstone by Applied Project must demonstrate the project's relevance to psychological principles, its potential or observed impact, and evidence of rigorous evaluation. This report should also detail the student's involvement and implementation of the program, offering insights or recommendations for future application or research.

Students may also choose to work with a Non-Academic Advisor, such as a mental health practitioner or community organizer, to gain additional support and expertise in the development and implementation of their project. This advisor must be approved by the student's primary and secondary academic advisors from the Psychology program.

In summary, the Capstone by Applied Project provides a structured framework for students to engage with mental health issues in a practical, impactful way, offering a range of resources and support mechanisms to facilitate effective treatment and intervention strategies.

### Question 84: Where can I get the information about motorcycle parking?  
### Answer: 

The information about motorcycle parking can be found online. Local government websites often have sections dedicated to parking rules and regulations, including those specific to motorcycles. Additionally, some cities may have specific motorcycle parking maps or guides available online. These resources can provide detailed information about designated motorcycle parking spots, rules, and any restrictions that might apply. If you're looking for information about a specific area, you might also consider contacting local parking authorities or visiting local government offices for more personalized assistance.

### Question 85: Where can I find resources to facilitate my graduate program after Fulbright undergraduate?  
### Answer: 

After completing the Fulbright University Vietnam (FUV) undergraduate program, students can find resources to facilitate their graduate studies in several ways. Firstly, they can leverage the connections and networks they have built during their time at FUV, including faculty members who may have recommendations for graduate programs or could serve as references. Secondly, FUV itself may have partnerships with other universities and research institutions that could provide pathways to graduate studies. Additionally, students can apply for scholarships and fellowships, such as the Fulbright Scholarship itself, which could fund their graduate education. They can also access FUV's career services and alumni network for guidance on graduate school applications and for potential leads on programs that align with their interests in Vietnam Studies or related fields. Furthermore, students can explore external funding opportunities, such as those offered by governmental or non-governmental organizations, to support their graduate education. Lastly, FUV's student research fund and other financial aid options may still be available to support students as they transition into graduate studies, depending on the specific policies and availability at the time of application.

### Question 86: Can you give me information about teaching assistant program right now?  
### Answer: 

The teaching assistant program is a crucial component of the educational process, designed to support and enhance the learning experience for both students and instructors. Teaching assistants (TAs) play a vital role in the classroom, often assisting with course delivery, facilitating discussions, grading assignments, and providing additional support to students.

In most academic institutions, the teaching assistant program is structured to provide graduate students with valuable teaching experience and professional development opportunities. TAs are typically selected based on their academic performance, relevant experience, and a demonstrated interest in education. They are often paired with faculty members who supervise and mentor them throughout the term.

The responsibilities of a teaching assistant can vary depending on the course and the institution. Common duties include:

- Leading discussion sections or recitation sessions
- Grading assignments and exams
- Holding office hours for students to seek help and guidance
- Assisting the instructor with course preparation and administration
- Providing feedback to students on their work
- Organizing and supervising laboratory sessions or other practical components of the course

Participation in a teaching assistant program can significantly benefit graduate students by:

- Developing their teaching skills and pedagogical knowledge
- Gaining practical experience in a classroom setting
- Enhancing their communication and interpersonal skills
- Building a professional network within their academic field
- Contributing to their own academic and professional development

For students enrolled in a course with a teaching assistant, the presence of a TA can offer additional support and resources, potentially improving their learning outcomes. TAs can provide explanations in a different style, offer extra help outside of regular class times, and create a more interactive and engaging learning environment.

In summary, the teaching assistant program is an integral part of the academic ecosystem, providing valuable support to both students and faculty while also offering graduate students a pathway to professional growth and development. The specifics of the program can vary widely depending on the institution, the department, and the individual course, so it's important to consult the relevant course information or departmental guidelines for detailed information.

The references provided do not directly address the current state of teaching assistant programs, as they pertain to a course information request form and do not contain specific data or descriptions about the program itself. Therefore, the information provided above is based on general knowledge about teaching assistant programs and their functions within an academic setting.

### Question 88: How can I get the information of campus usage for events so that I can have proper place to study without getting interrupted?  
### Answer: 

To get the information of campus usage for events so that you can have a proper place to study without getting interrupted, you should follow these steps:

1. **Contact the Event Coordinator**: Reach out to the person or office responsible for scheduling events on campus. This could be the Office of Student Activities, the Dean's Office, or a specific department that handles event planning.

2. **Check the University Calendar**: Regularly check the university's official calendar or website for upcoming events. This will give you an idea of when and where events are taking place.

3. **Use Online Scheduling Tools**: Some universities have online tools or platforms where you can check the availability of classrooms, study spaces, and other areas for booking study sessions.

4. **Talk to Your Academic Advisor**: Your academic advisor may have insights into the campus schedule and can offer advice on the best times and places to study.

5. **Visit the Library or Quiet Study Spaces**: Libraries and designated quiet study areas are often less affected by events. Check their schedules for any events that might impact your study time.

6. **Sign Up for Notifications**: If available, sign up for event notifications from the university. This way, you'll receive updates about upcoming events that might affect your study schedule.

7. **Flexible Study Schedule**: Be flexible with your study schedule. If you know an event is happening in a particular area, consider studying in another location.

8. **Respectful Communication**: If you find that an event is regularly interrupting your study, consider reaching out to the event organizers respectfully to express your concerns and seek solutions.

By following these steps, you should be able to gather the necessary information and make informed decisions about where and when to study on campus, minimizing interruptions from events.

### Question 89: I used to take an undergraduate program at another university and I want to transfer credit of studied courses at that university. What should I do?  
### Answer: 

When applying for Credit Transfer, a student is responsible for providing all the information that is requested about the course(s) for which they are applying to transfer. Information may include but not limited to course curriculum, learning outcomes, course content, and assessments. To apply for Credit Transfer or an Exemption, students should submit an Application for Credit Transfer, along with the required information on the course(s), to the Office of the Registrar. The Registrar will coordinate with the Office of the Dean to determine whether credit or an exemption is justified.

### Question 90: What are the policies of CWP?  
### Answer: 

The policies of CWP are as follows: 1.7 Passing 70-72.9%. ADDITIONAL REQUIREMENTS AND EXCEPTIONS: This policy is applied university-wide. ### Question 91: I'm a student athlete then how can I bypass all of physical education courses required to graduate?  
### Answer: 

As a student athlete, you may be exempt from some or all of the physical education courses required by the Ministry of Education and Training (MOET) regulations. Here's how you can potentially bypass these requirements:

1. **Athletic Participation**: If you are actively participating in a varsity sport, you may be exempt from physical education courses based on your athletic involvement. Check with your university's athletic department to see if this exemption applies to you.

2. **Course Substitution**: Some universities allow students to substitute athletic participation for physical education courses. This means that your athletic training and competitions could count towards fulfilling the physical education requirement. Discuss this option with your academic advisor.

3. **Double Counting**: Since you are already taking a significant number of credits related to your sport, you might be able to double count some of these credits towards both your athletic program and your degree requirements. This would allow you to use those credits to meet other degree requirements instead of physical education.

4. **Consult with Advisors**: It is crucial to consult with both your academic advisor and your athletic advisor to understand all the options available to you. They can help you navigate the university's policies and procedures to ensure you meet all academic requirements while managing your athletic commitments.

5. **Review University Policies**: Familiarize yourself with the university's policies regarding physical education requirements and athletic exemptions. Each institution may have different rules and procedures.

6. **Petition Process**: If there is no automatic exemption, you may need to petition the university to waive the physical education requirement based on your athletic participation. This usually involves submitting a formal request with supporting documentation, such as a letter from your coach or athletic director.

7. **Alternative Courses**: If exemptions are not possible, consider taking alternative courses that could be more flexible with your schedule, such as online courses or courses offered during the summer or intersession.

Remember that while you may be exempt from physical education courses, you still need to meet the overall credit requirements for graduation. Make sure to plan your course schedule carefully to accommodate your athletic commitments and academic responsibilities.

### Question 93: Can you give me the procedure to request for funds to support club activities?  
### Answer: 

To request funds to support club activities at the university, follow these steps:

1. **Identify the Need**: Clearly define the purpose and objectives of the club activity that requires funding. This could include organizing events, purchasing materials, or covering other expenses related to club activities.

2. **Research Available Funding Sources**: Check with the university's financial aid office, student affairs office, or the specific department that oversees student clubs and organizations. Many universities have dedicated funds for student clubs and organizations.

3. **Prepare a Proposal**: Develop a detailed proposal outlining the club activity, the budget required, how the funds will be used, and the expected outcomes or benefits of the activity. Include a timeline for the event or project and any other relevant information.

4. **Gather Supporting Documentation**: Compile any necessary supporting documentation, such as a budget breakdown, a list of expected expenses, and a plan for fundraising or cost-sharing if applicable.

5. **Submit the Proposal**: Submit the proposal to the appropriate office or committee responsible for allocating funds to student clubs and organizations. This may involve filling out an application form or presenting your proposal in person.

6. **Follow Up**: After submission, follow up with the office or committee to ensure they have received your proposal and to inquire about the review process and timeline.

7. **Review and Approval Process**: The proposal will be reviewed by a committee or designated individuals. They may request additional information or clarification before making a decision.

8. **Notification and Disbursement**: Once approved, you will be notified of the amount of funding allocated and how the funds will be disbursed. Follow the instructions provided for receiving the funds.

9. **Reporting and Accountability**: After the club activity has taken place, you may be required to submit a report detailing how the funds were used and the outcomes of the activity. This is to ensure accountability and transparency.

10. **Engage with Advisors**: Throughout the process, engage with your club advisors or faculty mentors for guidance and support in preparing the proposal and managing the funds.

It's important to note that the specific procedures and requirements may vary depending on the university's policies and available resources. Always consult with the relevant university office for the most accurate and up-to-date information.

Regarding the provided contexts, the procedure for requesting funds for club activities is not explicitly detailed, but the general process involves identifying the need, researching available funding sources, preparing a proposal, gathering supporting documentation, submitting the proposal, following up, going through a review and approval process, receiving notification and disbursement, and finally reporting on the use of funds and the outcomes of the activity. The contexts mention a student research fund which supports student’s research projects, including capstone projects, but the same general procedure would apply for requesting funds for club activities, with adjustments to the specifics of the proposal and the nature of the club activities.

### Question 94: How many ways are there provided by the university can I get the support in my academic path?  
### Answer: 

There are several ways the university provides support for students in their academic path. Firstly, students have access to labs, tools, and software relevant to their project work, which is crucial for practical learning and application of theoretical knowledge. Secondly, support is provided for learning new software or techniques where necessary, ensuring that students are not left to fend for themselves when encountering new challenges. Thirdly, mentorship and industry involvement are integral parts of the academic support system. Industry mentors may be available for project guidance, helping to bridge the gap between academic learning and industry practice. These mentors can serve as secondary advisors for capstone projects, participate in grading as either a secondary advisor or a member of the capstone panel, but they are not primary advisors or independent reviewers. Additionally, students can benefit from limited funding for materials and resources, which is crucial for practical projects. The university also provides policies on budgeting and purchasing to ensure responsible use of these funds. Lastly, the university emphasizes academic integrity, which is an essential part of any academic support system to ensure that students are guided in ethical conduct and responsible scholarship. In summary, the university offers a comprehensive support system that includes access to resources, support for learning new skills, mentorship from industry professionals, financial assistance, and a strong emphasis on academic integrity.

### Question 95: Can you give me the information about student fees and charges policy?  
### Answer: 

The undergraduate program at Fulbright University Vietnam (Fulbright) has a student fees and charges policy that is outlined in the "Fees & Charges Guide" for undergraduate students. According to this policy, students are expected to pay their tuition fees in a timely manner. If a student is unable to do so, they may request a late payment or an extension from Student Financial Services. However, with an outstanding balance, the student will be placed on a Financial Hold, which restricts their ability to register for new courses, participate in classes, or engage in a Work-Study Program during the current term.

The policy also states that before placing a student on a Financial Hold, the Student Financial Services team will attempt to determine the circumstances and request a timely response from the student. If the student anticipates being unable to clear the account on time, they should meet with the Student Financial Services team as soon as possible to request assistance and alternative solutions.

In the case of approved exceptional circumstances that prevent a student from fulfilling their financial obligations, tuition credit may be considered. These circumstances include exceptional medical circumstances, close bereavement, being a victim of a serious crime, disabilities where reasonable adjustments are not yet in place, and exceptional and unforeseeable transport difficulties. Supporting documentation and authorization from the course instructor(s), the student's academic/major advisor, and the Registrar's Office are required for such considerations.

Furthermore, the policy addresses course withdrawals due to exceptional circumstances. Students may request a tuition credit for courses they need to withdraw from due to these circumstances. However, no reduction in tuition is granted for withdrawals resulting in fewer than 12 academic credits. Students should also be aware that course withdrawals may affect their financial aid eligibility if they result in fewer than the minimum credits for full-time enrollment.

Regarding course registration and waitlists, the policy states that each course has a maximum capacity, and students can join a waitlist for courses that are full through the Fulbright One Stop portal. Students will be enrolled in the course in the order of their appearance on the waitlist during registration or Add/Drop time. When a waitlisted student is added to a course, it is the student's responsibility to ensure they are aware of and can meet the course requirements.

The document also notes that it will be updated regularly as needed, reflecting Fulbright University Vietnam's commitment to innovation and continuous improvement. Therefore, students are advised to regularly check the latest version of the policy for any updates.

### Question 97: I'm having some bad experience with a professor teaching a course. The problem was his way of delivering does not meet academic standard and I want to say something about this with people having higher authorities. What should I do?  
### Answer: 

You should first discuss the matter with the course instructor(s). If the matter remains unresolved and you believe there has been an error in grading, bias, or failure to follow published grading policies, you may follow the appeal process outlined in the academic policies of your institution. This typically involves submitting a Review of Final Grade Request form to the Registrar's Office within a specified timeframe. The Registrar's Office then informs the Dean’s Office, which may mediate the issue or organize a panel review for an independent evaluation of the grade. In cases concerning the interpretation of a course policy, the Dean’s Office will defer to the course syllabus whenever possible and otherwise will make a final ruling on the matter.

The appeal process is designed to ensure fairness and due process, so it's important to follow the steps outlined by your institution. However, if the issue is more about the teaching methodology or academic standards rather than a specific grade dispute, you should approach the situation differently.

For concerns about teaching methodology or academic standards:

1. **Document Everything**: Keep a detailed record of all interactions with the professor, including dates, times, and descriptions of incidents.

2. **Schedule a Meeting**: Request a meeting with the professor to discuss your concerns. Be specific about the issues and provide examples where possible.

3. **Seek Support**: If the meeting does not resolve the issue, consider seeking support from the department chair, academic advisor, or another faculty member within your department.

4. **Use Official Channels**: If the issue remains unresolved, you can escalate the matter through official channels such as the Dean's Office or the Office of Academic Affairs.

5. **Be Proactive**: Follow up on any actions taken and keep records of all communications.

6. **Fulbright Email**: Use your institutional email (Fulbright email, if applicable) for all communications to maintain a professional record.

7. **Be Prepared**: Before any meeting, prepare your concerns, data, and potential solutions. Remember, advisors are there to guide, not to do the work for you.

8. **Respect Time and Be Proactive**: Respect your professor's and advisors' time and be proactive in setting up meetings and following up on actionable items.

9. **Understand Requirements**: Clarify what is expected at each stage of your project or course, especially for a capstone.

10. **Change in Research Direction**: If you wish to change the research question or methodology, consult with your advisors and get their approval.

Remember, while it's important to address academic concerns, it's equally important to approach the situation professionally and constructively. The goal is to improve the educational experience and resolve the issue, not to create conflict.

After investigation, if the Deans can mediate, no further action is required. Otherwise, the Registrar's Office organizes a panel review with the Dean’s Office for an independent evaluation of the grade. The grade determined after this evaluation shall be the final grade. ### Question 98: I'm a third year student and don't know if I should do a capstone project then where should I go to get advice?  
### Answer: 

You should go to get advice from your advisor. At the beginning of the semester, you should meet with your advisor as early as possible and set a regular meeting schedule with your advisor. Consult your advisor on the specific deliverables they expect to see from you. Remember, the capstone should demonstrate original critical and creative thinking, and we encourage primary research. However, it should not require extensive fieldwork. You should think very carefully about an appropriate project for you, considering your interests and post-graduation plans. If you enjoy doing historical research and want an opportunity to carry out a long-term research project, the Capstone year provides time and guidance that is unparalleled by any course or other opportunity at the undergraduate level. However, if you wish to graduate with distinction but don't particularly enjoy doing independent research, you may want to skip the Capstone and focus on GPA honors instead.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: History Capstone Handbook - 2025-26.pdf, Page: 9]
The Capstone project is a year-long undertaking with less structure than a traditional course. It is certainly not the easiest way to complete your degree, and it may not be the most logical option for you, depending on your interests and your post-graduation plans. You should not consider it to be the default pathway to finishing your degree. One of the best reasons to undertake a Capstone project is if you enjoy doing historical research (which you will have sampled in Hands-On History and the research seminars you have completed) and want an opportunity to carry out a long-term research project. For such students, the Capstone year provides time and guidance that is unparalleled by any course or other opportunity at the undergraduate level. However, if you wish to graduate with distinction—an honorable goal— but you don’t particularly enjoy doing independent research, you may want to skip the Capstone and focus on GPA honors instead! ### Question 99: I'm a member of Fulbright Basketball Club and going to attend a tournament. I need the official transcript and asking for some absence in classes then where should I get help?  
### Answer: 

To request an excused absence for attending the tournament as a member of the Fulbright Basketball Club, you should follow these steps:

1. **Prepare the Necessary Documents**:
   - **Summary of the Program**: Write a summary (100-200 words) describing the tournament, its significance, and your role in the basketball club.
   - **Proof of Attendance**: Obtain an acceptance email, invitation letter, or any official document that confirms your participation in the tournament.
   - **Proof of Travel**: Secure your flight and accommodation information or itinerary to show your travel plans.

2. **Complete the Official Activity Excused Absence Request Form**:
   - **Form Submission**: The form must be completed by your faculty or supervising staff. They need to verify your academic standing with the Registrar’s Office before submitting the form.
   - **Form Details**: Fill in all the required information on the form, including your personal details, the name and location of the event, and the dates of departure and return.

3. **Submit the Request**:
   - **Submission to the Office**: Your faculty or supervising staff should submit the completed form to the Office of the Registrar, with copies to Academic Affairs and the Registrar’s Office for record.

4. **Inform Your Instructors**:
   - **Contact Instructors**: It is your responsibility to inform your instructors about the upcoming absence and make arrangements to make up any missed work.

5. **Follow Up After the Trip**:
   - **Reflection Paper**: Write a 300-500 words reflection paper about your experience at the tournament and submit it to ug.academic.affairs@fulbright.edu.vn no later than 7 days after returning.

6. **Register for Classes**:
   - **Registration**: Ensure you register for classes using the One-Stop platform for the term you return to, at least 24 hours prior to class time.

7. **Handling Unplanned Absences**:
   - **Discuss with Instructors**: If there are any unplanned absences or conflicts, discuss them with your instructors as soon as possible.

8. **Support from Academic Affairs and Registrar’s Office**:
   - **Emergency Assistance**: In case of an emergency such as hospitalization following an accident, contact the Academic Affairs team or Registrar’s Office during business hours.

By following these steps, you should be able to manage your absence for the tournament and maintain your academic responsibilities at Fulbright University. Remember, it is crucial to stay in good academic standing and to adhere to the university’s policies regarding absences and make-up work.
