### Question 101: How can I borrow books from the library?  
### Answer: 

You can borrow books from the library by visiting the library in person, searching the library's online catalog to find the books you need, locating the books on the shelves, checking them out at the circulation desk with your student ID, and following the library's borrowing policies regarding loan periods and renewals. If the books you need are not available in the library, you can also request them through interlibrary loan services, which allow you to borrow books from other libraries. Additionally, many libraries offer digital borrowing options, allowing you to access e-books and other digital resources online. Always make sure to return or renew your borrowed items on time to avoid late fees and to ensure that others have access to the resources you've borrowed.

### Question 102: How to work with major report?  
### Answer: 

The major report for a capstone project typically involves several key steps and components. Here's a structured approach to working on your major report:

1. **Understand the Requirements**: Carefully read and understand all the submission requirements provided by your institution or course. This includes the format, word count, structure, and any specific sections that need to be included.

2. **Plan Your Report**: Start by outlining the structure of your report. This typically includes an introduction, literature review, methodology, results, discussion, conclusion, and future work sections. Make sure to include all the required components such as the final design, simulation/prototype details, testing/experimental results, and appendices.

3. **Gather and Organize Information**: Collect all the necessary data, results, and analysis from your project work. Organize this information logically to support each section of your report.

4. **Write the Report**: Begin writing your report, focusing on clarity, coherence, and adherence to the specified format and style guidelines. Ensure that each section flows logically from the previous one.

5. **Executive Summary**: Write a concise and engaging executive summary that encapsulates the essence of your project. This is crucial as it is the first part of your report that readers will encounter.

6. **Review and Revise**: Once you have completed the first draft, review your report for clarity, coherence, and adherence to the submission requirements. Check for formatting, referencing, and any errors.

7. **Seek Feedback**: Share your draft with peers, advisors, or mentors and incorporate their feedback to improve the quality of your report.

8. **Finalize and Submit**: After making all necessary revisions, convert your Word document into a PDF and ensure all required appendices and documentation are included. Submit the final report according to the specified deadline.

9. **Prepare for Defense**: If there is a presentation or defense component, prepare accordingly. This includes practicing your presentation, being ready to answer questions, and possibly revising your report based on feedback during the Q&A session.

Remember, the major report is a culmination of your capstone project work, so take the time to present your findings clearly, critically, and professionally. Attention to detail and adherence to guidelines will be crucial for a successful submission.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: HCE_Capstone_Handbook_Final_2025.01.16.pdf, Page: 5]
followed by up to 10 minutes for Q&A with the judging panel and audience. • Submission Requirements: ▪ Final report: Submit your individual report on Canvas and provide a copy to the judging panel members at least 7 days before the last day of the semester. ### Question 103: How many way can I fill in the requirements of EL?  
### Answer: 

All full-time, undergraduate, degree-seeking students must complete at least 04 credits and a maximum of 12 credits under the ELP as a graduation requirement.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: CS_Capstone_Guideline_v2_Dec_20_2024.pdf, Page: 2]

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 20]
count toward elective or major requirements (upon advisor approval). Fulbright’s Experiential Learning Program (ELP) exists to create, standardize, and facilitate academic credit-bearing experiential learning experiences. All full-time, undergraduate, degree- seeking students must complete at least 04 credits and a maximum of 12 credits under the ELP as a graduation requirement. Current ELP streams are housed within Academic Affairs (AA), Career Services (CS), and Center for Entrepreneurship and Innovation (CEI), where each team is responsible for administrative and academic duties of their respective stream(s). The ELP operates within Fulbright’s undergraduate program’s standard operating procedures and is developed in consultation with undergraduate program leadership and faculty. For more details, please refer here https://onestop.fulbright.edu.vn/s/article/Experiential-Learning- Program 13.5  Electives To complete the degree, students are free to take elective courses from the Course Catalogue.
